## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task asks for the rate of change of concentration dA_dt given time t and current concentration A, which is a classic differential rate law problem in reaction kinetics where the reaction rate is typically a function of reactant concentration, and time-dependent rate coefficients may appear in non-isothermal or catalyst deactivation scenarios.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate of consumption independent of A)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration, exponential decay)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration, bimolecular reaction)
- n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence on concentration)
- Reversible first-order reaction (A ⇌ B, A0 fixed): dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (linear combination of concentration and constant, representing forward and backward rates)
- Autocatalytic / logistic rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (quadratic polynomial, describing autocatalysis or logistic growth of product)
- Phase-boundary controlled (contracting sphere): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A)**c2 (fractional conversion dependence, e.g., c2=2/3 for contracting volume)
- Time-dependent rate constant (catalyst deactivation): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant decays or grows exponentially with time)
- Power-law time-dependent rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (rate coefficient varies with time as a power law)
- Diffusion-controlled decay: dA_dt = c0 / (c1 + t)**c2 (rate depends explicitly on time, e.g., parabolic law with c2=1/2)
- Concentration-dependent inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation-like decrease of rate with increasing concentration, similar to Michaelis-Menten but for substrate consumption)
- Nucleation-and-growth (Avrami) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * exp(c2 * t**c3) (rate explicit in t, typical for solid-state transformations without explicit A dependence)
- Autocatalytic with pre-factor: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic differential equation, symmetric quadratic form)
- Fractional conversion with time shift: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) / (t + c2) (mixed explicit time and concentration dependence)
- Second-order reversible: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (full quadratic in A for multiple competing elementary steps)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order test: If dA_dt scales as a power of A, try dA_dt = c0 * A**c1; fractional c1 suggests complex kinetics
- Reversibility: A near-constant linear combination of A with an intercept suggests equilibrium between forward and reverse steps
- Autocatalysis signature: Rate initially increases with A then decreases, modeled by quadratic A + A**2 terms or A*(c1-A)
- Solid-state phase boundaries: Rate dependent on (1 - A) raised to a fraction (e.g., 1/2, 2/3) suggests contracting geometry or diffusion in product layer
- Deactivation/inhibition: If rate slows faster than concentration decay alone, multiply by exp(-c*t) or rational factor like 1/(1+c*A)
- Diffusion-limited reactions: Rate inversely related to time, often dA_dt ~ t**-c (0 < c < 1) when A follows a power-law relaxation
- Nucleation processes: Explicit time dependence with no direct A dependence, often a bell-shaped rate curve with t**n * exp(-t**m) structure
- Shifted equilibrium: Rate contains (A - c) indicating a non-zero asymptotic concentration, useful for product-inhibited or reversible systems
- Sigmoidal consumption curves imply dA_dt has a maximum at intermediate A, suggesting autocatalytic or logistic-like forms
- Composite rate laws: Sum of several elementary rate contributions (e.g., zero-order background plus first-order main reaction) give linear combinations
